Free Talk

Nostalgia 245

— and More

I want to praise some people of the past, which is probably not [a love of skeletons].

The so-called people of the past refer to the so-called "new party" in the late Guangxu period. In the early Republic of China, they were called the "old new party." After the defeat in the Sino-Japanese War, they considered themselves enlightened and wanted to "reform." Even middle-aged people in their thirties and forties were reading [Practical Arithmetic Talks] and [Chemical Mirror Origins]. They also wanted to learn English and Japanese, reciting with stiff tongues and strange voices, without any sense of shame. The goal was to read [foreign books] because they wanted to bring [wealth and power] to China. Even now, old book stalls occasionally have [Wealth and Power Series] appearing, just like the current [Descriptive Dictionary] [Basic English], which were products of that era. Even Zhang Zhidong, who came from the eight-legged essay, also asked Miao Quansun to compile [Booklist Answers] for him and tried his best to add various translations, showing the intensity of the [reform] trend.

However, the current phenomenon is different. Some new youths have a situation that is exactly the opposite of the [old new party]. They have not been contaminated by the eight-legged essay at all, and they come from schools, but they are not experts in national studies. However, they have begun to learn seal script, fill in lyrics, and encourage people to read [Zhuangzi] and [Literary Selections]. Their envelopes also have self-carved printing plates, and their poems are also written in square characters. Except for their fondness for writing new poems, they are simply like elegant people in the early Guangxu period, except that they lack braids and sometimes wear Western clothes.

Recently, there is a common saying: [Old bottles cannot hold new wine]. This is actually inaccurate. Old bottles can hold new wine, and new bottles can also hold old wine. If you don't believe it, try swapping a bottle of Wujiapi and a bottle of brandy. The Wujiapi in the brandy bottle is still Wujiapi. This simple experiment not only shows the style of [Wugeng Tune] [Zan Shi Zi], but also allows new content to be put into it, and it also confirms that the shell of the new youth can hide the minions of [Tongcheng Heresy] or [Literary Deviants].

Although the vision of the [old new party] was shallow, they had one purpose: to seek wealth and power. Therefore, they were firm and practical. Although their foreign language was strange, they had one purpose: to seek the art of wealth and power. Their seriousness was genuine and enthusiastic. When the anti-Manchu theory spread, many people became revolutionaries, still because they wanted to bring wealth and power to China and believed that this must begin with anti-Manchuism.

Anti-Manchuism has long been successful, and the May Fourth Movement has long passed. Seal script, lyrics, [Zhuangzi], [Literary Selections], ancient-style envelopes, and square-character new poems. Now we have new attempts to establish ourselves in the world with [classical elegance]. If we can really establish ourselves, that would add a new example to [the struggle for survival].

Re-Discussing Opium 246

— Yu Zhan

Yesterday, I visited Mr. Zhao Yuchuan, and he showed me the ninth volume of the Wan Guo Gong Bao (The Chinese Recorder) from 1889. It contained an article about opium, written by someone named Joseph Edkins. This gentleman discussed opium from the perspectives of Greece, Latin countries, and Arabia, to China. The article was quite long, five or six thousand words, with numerous references. I suspect he is a Westerner with a deep understanding of Chinese studies. If he is Chinese, then he is also quite knowledgeable in Western learning.

During the Sui and Tang Dynasties in China, the Arabs established the Great Arabian Empire. They highly valued Greek medicine for treating various diseases, and opium was among the medicines used. The ancient Greek pharmacologist Dioscorides, in his compilation of ten thousand medicinal materials, indeed mentioned that opium had the effects of calming the nerves, relieving pain, and aiding eye recovery.

The Arabian Empire began trading with China during the reign of Emperor Taizong of Tang. Arab merchants sailed to Guangzhou and other seaports, bringing goods such as ivory, frankincense, pig iron, cotton, borneol, white sugar, glassware, rose water, and various medicinal materials for trade. Poppy seeds were likely among the medicinal materials. Based on the situation in Europe, it is likely that China had not yet encountered poppy flowers before that time. It is also called "Mi Xiang Hua" (Rice Fragrance Flower) because its fruit resembles a sac, and its seeds resemble rice, hence the name.

During the reign of Emperor Minghuang of Tang, Chen Zangqi mentioned the words of Song Yangzi, saying that poppies have four petals, red and white, with light red halos. The seed pod is shaped like a sac, and the arrows used by archers contain fine grains. Additionally, Guo 　Tuo's "Book on Planting Trees" of the Tang Dynasty states that planting poppies on the ninth day of the ninth lunar month or during the Mid-Autumn Festival will result in larger flowers and fuller seeds (see the Compilation of Illustrations and Writings from the Complete Collection of Ancient and Modern Books, Section on Plants and Trees, Examination of Poppy Seed Department and Flower Department). According to Liu Zongyuan's biography of Guo 　Tuo, it can be confirmed that Guo 　also lived during the prosperous Tang Dynasty, around the same time as Chen Zangqi. From Emperor Taizong to Emperor Minghuang, a century passed, and the Arabian Empire had been trading with China for a long time. China already knew how to cultivate poppies, which is entirely plausible.

In the sixth year of the Kai Bao era of Emperor Taizu of Song, he ordered Liu Han, a pharmacist, and nine Daoist priests, including Ma Zhi, to revise the Kai Bao Materia Medica. They referred to poppies as "Ying Zi Su" (Poppy Seed Millet), also known as "Mi Nang Zi" (Rice Sac Seed) and "Yu Mi" (Imperial Rice). It was also stated that its grains mainly treat the movement of Dan Shi (cinnabar), loss of appetite. It can be cooked with bamboo sap into a porridge that is extremely delicious. Furthermore, Emperor Renzong of Song ordered all counties and prefectures to illustrate the medicinal materials produced locally, following the example of Emperor Gaozong of Tang who ordered the Duke of Ying Guo to compile the Tang Materia Medica. He specifically instructed Su Song, a doctor of the Imperial Academy, to compile and narrate the illustrated Materia Medica. This book stated that poppy flowers are found everywhere, and people often plant them for decoration. There are two types, red and white flowers, with a slight fishy smell. The fruit is shaped like a bottle, and the seeds are extremely fine like grains of rice. Gardeners fertilize the soil every other year, sow the seeds in the ninth month, and the seedlings begin to grow after winter and into spring, growing very lushly. Otherwise, they will not grow, or they will not thrive. They are harvested when the pods turn yellow. It also stated that poppy seed porridge can be used to treat vomiting and regurgitation, using three he of white poppy seeds, three qian of ginseng powder, and five cun of finely chopped fresh yam, grinding the three ingredients together. Add two sheng and three he of water to extract six he, then add fresh ginger juice and a little salt, mix well, and take in divided doses, regardless of the time of day, without interfering with other decoctions or pills. Moreover, during the Zhenghe era of Emperor Huizong of Song, Kou Zongshi, a medical official, wrote "Danyan Yanyi Materia Medica," briefly stating that poppy seeds are cold in nature, and excessive consumption can lead to bowel movements. Grind and boil them in water, add honey to make a soup, which is very suitable for drinking. Other works, such as Yang Shi Ying's "Zhi Zhi Fang" (Direct Pointers), Wang Qiu's "Bai Yi Xuan Fang" (Hundred and One Selected Prescriptions), and Wang Shuo's "Yi Jian Fang" (Simple Prescriptions), all state that poppy shells are effective in treating dysentery. Based on the above statements, it can be proven that people in the Song Dynasty already used poppy seeds or their shells to boil soup and make pills to treat diseases, considering it a precious product for treating dysentery. As for Song poems that mention poppies, in addition to the poems by Su Shi and Su Zhe mentioned earlier, there is also a seven-character quatrain by Xie Yu, praising poppy flowers:

Lead paste delicately dots the flower tips,

It is said that spring is deep and the snow has not melted.

A hu of a thousand sacs of pale jade millet,

The east wind blows, making the rice grow long waists.

Jin Liuhe's "Xuan Ming Fang" treats chronic coughs and night sweats with two and a half liang of poppy shells, removing the stems and membranes, stir-fried with vinegar, taking one liang, and half a liang of black plum, baked into powder. Take two qian per dose, taken with white soup at bedtime. Furthermore, Li Gao said that poppy capsules have the effect of astringing and solidifying qi, and can enter the kidneys, so they are especially suitable for treating bone diseases. Additionally, Wei Yilin's "De Xiao Fang" treats chronic diarrhea that does not stop, using poppy shells to remove the tendons, roasted with honey into powder, taking five fen per dose, taken with honey soup, which is effective. Moreover, Zhu Zhenheng said that nowadays people with consumption cough often use poppy shells to stop bleeding, and those with damp-heat dysentery use them to stop astringency. Although its curative effect is urgent, it kills people like a sword, so caution should be taken. Based on the above statements, it can be seen that during the Jin and Yuan dynasties, poppy shells were not only used to treat dysentery but also used to treat coughs and bone diseases. As for Zhu Zhenheng's statement that it kills people like a sword, so caution should be taken, it can be seen that at that time, there were already people who had died from opium poisoning. As for its appearance in literature, Feng Zizhen's "Eighteen Rhapsodies" states, "Some wear poppies after the rain, or frost-covered chrysanthemum flowers," indicating that poppy flowers were also used for ornamental purposes.

A Way to Relieve Boredom 247

— Bi

Are you bored?

[What if I am bored?] you might retort.

As long as you are willing to retort, I have something to say, because I know what to do when bored. I have a plan to relieve boredom.

For example, if you feel extremely tired and bored, and don't know what to do, just feeling listless, then you can go out. Outside the door, there will always be examples of people who are not bored.

When you first step out, your steps will undoubtedly be heavy, and you will have to drag them. But after dragging for a while, you will suddenly hear a sound, a very leisurely sound, floating lightly from who knows where. So you look up and see a huqin seller walking towards you. You see him pulling the bow, with many huqins of various sizes on his back. Although he is in such a busy city, he doesn't look at anything or anyone, just playing a clear and fluent tune, with an attitude of complete nonchalance.

[If only I had such a huqin,] you might suddenly realize, [I would naturally be able to be nonchalant too.]

Since that's the case, why shouldn't you also have such a huqin? You have no reason not to have one, so you get one too.

And so, from then on, you also play your huqin, and your boredom is dispelled. You can also not look at anything or anyone, just play, with an attitude of nonchalance. [Learning to be like a huqin seller,] you finally confirm, [is definitely not a difficult thing; why not learn something so easy and continue to be bored?]

Because you have already realized this yourself, you can't understand why other people are still bored. Maybe it's because they don't see through things like you do, and they are preoccupied with the gains and losses of food and clothing. The only ones who see through things, besides yourself, are the huqin seller, you believe. You believe he also feels extremely [tired] and [bored], which is why he plays the huqin on the street in such a leisurely and [nonchalant] way. Also, it's not just the huqin that can dispel boredom, but also books, lovers, the clouds in the sky, and the wildflowers by the roadside. If you lose faith in A today, you can have faith in B tomorrow... as long as you are flexible, you will always find an object that will make you no longer bored.

The Headsman's Fee 248

— Zi

Two militiamen, escorting Chun Sheng's corpse, carried it from afar into the house. Aunt Shao Yun's heart felt as if it had been dug out. With a loud cry, she spat out a pool of fresh blood.

"My ill-fated child!..."

She only cried out this sentence before rolling around, hugging the blood-soaked body. The deceased's head had been thrown far away to the side.

For a long while, she remained silent. Most of the relatives and neighbors who had gathered to watch secretly wiped away tears. No one spoke, watching Aunt Shao Yun collapse beside the corpse.

"What's going on?" The clan chief ran out from the crowd and kicked Aunt Shao Yun forcefully. "Aren't you getting up yet? Who told you to raise such an unfilial son?"

Aunt Shao Yun stared blankly, unable to speak.

"Bring water!" The clan chief ordered.

With a gentle spray, Aunt Shao Yun began to cry again.

"My son!..."

"Don't cry!" The clan chief threatened. "There are still two deputy masters waiting for your reply!"

Aunt Shao Yun truly dared not cry out loud anymore. She stared at the clan chief. "The deputy masters say," the clan chief raised his voice, "according to the regulations of the headquarters... for each local prisoner executed, there is a headsman's fee of twenty yuan..."

"Headsman's fee?" Aunt Shao Yun was stunned again. She didn't even have enough money for Chun Sheng's coffin.

"Also," the clan chief continued, "Chun Sheng was imprisoned for twenty-three days, with a daily food cost of three jiao, totaling nine yuan and nine jiao. The total cost, including the headsman's fee, is thirty yuan. You must hand it all over to the deputy masters to take away!"

Aunt Shao Yun was even more speechless. She got up and kowtowed three times to the clan chief.

"Clan Elder Chang San, where am I going to get the money? I don't even have money for Chun Sheng's coffin yet..."

"Who told you to raise such an unfilial son?"

Aunt Shao Yun's heart felt like it was about to explode. She wanted to bite the clan chief, but...

"Don't have it?" The two militiamen also stood up. "Then you can hand over a relative for us to take away first! We'll release him when your money arrives... "

"Clan Elder Chang San!"

The clan chief shook his head repeatedly.

"There's nothing I can do!"

So, her younger son, Tai Sheng, was dragged out of the crowd by the militiamen.

"Go!" The militiamen struck Tai Sheng's unwilling legs; then turned back to Aunt Shao Yun. "Please send the money quickly, or it will be another three jiao a day!"

Aunt Shao Yun had completely gone mad. She shouted at the clan chief, she cried to the heavens, she rolled around hugging her eldest son Chun Sheng's corpse.

The relatives and neighbors all shed tears of sorrow.

At night, the relatives and neighbors came to help her prepare her eldest son for burial. For her younger son, for the thirty yuan headsman's fee and food expenses, Aunt Shao Yun became more and more distraught.

Heavens!

Finally... she hanged herself in the middle of the night!

September of the twenty-second year, the third anniversary of my aunt's death.

The Closed Door (2) 250

— By Henri de Régnier, translated by Li Wanjv

Every day during tea time, I saw the Tourlans sitting in the lobby of the hotel, always in those two old seats not far from the door. This door seemed to interest Mr. Tourlan very much. Around six o'clock, the door opened; the porter came in with the mail and placed a bundle of newspapers in front of Mr. Tourlan, and he quickly grabbed them. How quickly he tore off the seal and unfolded the large printed sheets! ... As he quickly looked at the newspaper, his wife attentively watched him. Sometimes Mr. Tourlan would hand a newspaper to her and point out a few lines of news for her to read. This couple amazed me every time I saw this scene. Who was this Mr. Tourlan, so concerned with current events? Did some people in the world really have nothing to do with everything except for the memories of lost happiness!

However, the stay in Riva gradually made me feel depressed, and I decided to continue my journey. The day before departure, I rented a small boat and spent some time on the lake. I felt that the sound of the oars seemed to soothe my pain and annoyance. I didn't return to the hotel until tea time. As I stepped into the main hall, the porter was handing a bundle of newspapers to Mr. Tourlan. He had only unfolded one and read a few words when I saw his face suddenly turn pale. His hands trembled. A violent emotion completely disturbed him. Suddenly, he stood up and went out. Mrs. Tourlan followed him. The newspaper remained on the table. I walked over. It was a "Political News" section. The front page had a large headline describing a tumultuous parliamentary meeting. The Foreign Minister gave a speech that resulted in the downfall of the cabinet. Some external difficulties led to this cabinet change, which also meant a political upheaval affecting the whole country.

Neither Mr. nor Mrs. Tourlan came out for dinner. After finishing my meal, I went to the lakeside to smoke a cigarette. The weather at night was warm and gentle, and I listened to the sound of the rippling waves for a long time, and watched a round yellow full moon slowly rise from the horizon. After I finished my cigarette, I walked back to the hotel. In the main hall, there were two Englishmen who had just arrived that morning, drinking "whiskey." I didn't wake the dozing porter, and climbed the wide stairs, walked along the corridor that passed in front of the Tourlans' room and led directly to my bedroom. As I approached their room, I faintly heard some excited, unusual voices. I stopped and listened carefully. It was Mr. Tourlan's voice, but his voice had changed, becoming rough and loud. The silent space was filled with the echoes of this voice. It was the tone of a speaker, an orator, magnificent, practiced, and uttered to incite the masses. I can assure you... in this desolate and deserted inn, hearing such a voice from behind this closed door was indeed a strange thing.

Talking Points

Diplomas and Bread 274

— Guang Han

It is no accident that diplomas are related to bread.

A person steps from home into school, what about the Book of Poetry? What about ABCD? What about three plus six equals nine? Vaguely, muddling through so many years; the fathers and brothers at home spent several hundred or several thousand dollars, fulfilling a wish to cultivate their children; from the principal to the teachers and staff to the tea boy in the school, everyone received a salary, and also unloaded some of the responsibility of educating students; and we ourselves, obtained a paper diploma that we had been dreaming of, and also fulfilled the obligation of studying hard. Everyone achieved perfect merit and everything was auspicious!

When a person with a diploma rolls from school into society, the first thing to do is to make a living. Making a living is another name for grabbing bread. Thus, diplomas become related to bread. A certain cigarette paper shop wants to hire apprentices, the level must be elementary school graduation; a certain company wants to recruit clerks, the knowledge must be middle school graduation; a certain bookstore intends to hire editors, the qualification must be university graduation. The so-called level, knowledge, and qualification, the representative object is of course the diploma.

Because eating bread requires a diploma, the things of society cheating diplomas, buying diplomas, forging diplomas, and selling diplomas arise in response to the times. In order to supply social demand.

But having a diploma does not necessarily mean having bread to eat. Under these circumstances, the diploma inevitably becomes an unfulfilled piece of waste paper. It is useless to hide it, and it is a pity to abandon it, and it is like chicken ribs. There are various reasons for having a diploma but not being able to eat bread... supply exceeds demand in society, not being good at promotion, lacking traction, no background, having a real diploma but no real skills, etc.

Indeed. It is no accident that diplomas are related to bread.

A Farce of Solving the Problem of Eating 275

— Li Li

The problem of eating is the most important and urgent problem for anyone who wants to eat and can eat. We who rely on school life may not have to find food ourselves to have food to eat—because we have not entered the path of adulthood and cannot be economically independent, we can open our mouths to eat our parents' blood and sweat, like chicks waiting to be fed. We are still young!? For us commuting students, lunch is a problem that can become a problem. Although the mother cooks the rice early and smiles as she waits for us to go back and gobble it up. But, the journey is far and it is too inconvenient to go back and forth! Let's have lunch at school? It is really difficult to get used to the tasteless rice and vegetables, so eating becomes a problem!

In the first few days, we brought some bread and biscuits to fill our hungry stomachs, but the sweet and dry taste was really difficult to swallow, so we desperately drank water, and forcibly poured the bread and biscuits into our throats like the Yellow River bursting its banks.

Under the guidance of an old classmate, we asked the school janitor to buy wontons, noodles and other kinds of wet snacks to chew on in the classroom—because the girls are tender-faced, it is very embarrassing to be seen by the teachers in the dining hall—together to promote, everyone followed suit, so the classroom became a dining hall... [Spoons and chopsticks qi Hong, sipping soup and sucking noodles correspond.]

When the number of people increased, it was inevitable to be slow, and often the class bell had already rung, and there were still people eating at the table. When they heard the bell ringing, they were shocked and at a loss, spilling soup and dropping chopsticks in a mess. If the cow is stubborn, it will go to the door. Is there an elegant small seat in the secluded inclined bridge for you to drink slowly? Only that small noodle restaurant in the style of a two-meat shop, buying wontons, steamed buns, no rice—this is where the working class solves the problem of eating, cheap and plentiful—the taste is not good—a bowl of old noodles for twelve copper yuan, a bowl of wontons for ten copper yuan, and a meat filling steamed bun for three copper yuan, which cannot be turned into two maos, and after eating three patterns, the stomach can be filled to the brim to go back.

Honestly, this dirty and narrow little noodle restaurant, I wouldn't even look at it on weekdays, let alone eat anything. But in desperation, there is no way, can't solve the problem of eating, and can't stand the meat riot—hunger—we finally stepped into this short, narrow and unclean little noodle restaurant, relying on the large number of people to cover our faces, and it didn't feel embarrassing, so you want wontons, I want noodles, he wants soup, and we yelled for a while like a hundred birds singing. We sat down on the narrow and crowded long bench, picked up the rough and unpolished Maozhu chopsticks, held up the blue flower coarse porcelain bowl, and ate it with a hula hula sound, which was also unique. The deserted and dirty little noodle restaurant, decorated with a group of innocent and lively little angels, is so lively, brilliant and energetic, attracting the attention of passersby.

This is the time for lunch. The working class, who solved the problem of eating in the small noodle restaurant, dragged their tired and heavy bodies into the small noodle restaurant as usual. The familiar table and benches with holes in the blue cloth shirt and trousers were replaced by white shirts and black skirts, which was a miracle for them. They scanned us with lost and suspicious eyes, sat down at the table near the door, and asked for a bowl of noodles with three additions—the three additions were pickled vegetables—and finished it in a whirlwind. This small bowl of noodles probably cannot fill the dry stomach that has been squeezed by labor. Annoyed, I stared at them blankly, letting the white air rising above the wontons slowly lower.

A delicate (?) young lady is eating with the rude (?) working class. Is it a strange phenomenon in the current society where class concepts have not been broken?

Traitor Merchants Dumped Japanese Goods Acted as Accomplices

Laziness 276

— Unknown

I can't recall which year it was, but it was an autumn time when the plantain trees were green and the air crisp.

Home—in the floating of the night, a small corner of a cramped, dim pavilion. Ah Shun's mother, an elderly woman with a bald spot and thinning white hair, sat alone under the dim light of a kerosene lamp, hunched over, her back curved. Her ten withered fingers stitched away at Ah Shun's worn-out, earth-toned short coat, the sleeve of which was torn. Fatigue had seized the elderly woman's deeply wrinkled, pale face. Her unnatural yawns… labored coughs; faint sighs, intermittent at the edges of her bloodless lips, sounded like a low, fragmented, chaotic dirge at the bottom of the night!

It was midnight! On the deserted streets, the sound of footsteps was rarely heard in the stillness.

[Ah Shun, go to sleep early. Uncle San will come first thing tomorrow morning to take you to the XX store!] The elderly woman's voice, like cracking bamboo, urged.

Sleep, young Ah Shun thought… as if it were something he didn't need right now! Although his eyelids felt as if they were being weighed down by something heavy, he ultimately didn't want his mother to be doing work alone in the dimness of night.

[Sleep! Ah Shun,] the elderly woman urged impatiently, eventually causing him to wrinkle his brow, leave his mother's embrace, go to bed, close his eyes, and toss and turn, unable to sleep.

Worried feelings, sorrowful experiences, in his complex memories, stirred up deep melancholy! He thought… years of unconscious drifting, wandering! Everything seemed to be dyed a deep gray! Tears, these seemingly familiar tears, on the pillow, in Ah Shun's eyes, uncontrollably flowed! Each one like a clear, mixed pearl carrying a bitter smile!

The next morning, Uncle San had already arrived at his home.

[Uncle San, good morning, please sit,] the sleepy-eyed elderly woman wiped the dust off the stool, poured a cup of scalding hot tea from the hot water vendor for Uncle San from the table, a slight smile on the corners of her eyes, yet the elderly woman's deeply wrinkled, pale face looked even more [feeble]! Her fleshless cheeks, protruding, frightening cheekbones, and somewhat dry ears, like a crisscrossing outline, clearly hinted at the onset of an eye disease.

[Alright, Ah Shun's mother,] Uncle San stretched in a long yawn.

The elderly woman stared earnestly at Ah Shun's thin body moving before her.

[Ah Shun, when you get there, you must listen to people!] she said…

[You should soften your temper a little!]

[Your…]

Page 20

[Mom, I understand everything, don't worry!] Ah Shun's childish heart, emotionally, simply couldn't speak.

Leaving home, stepping lightly on the sidewalk.

The dawn of the metropolis, in the roars of the tall factory chimneys, crawled out of the dark grave, spitting flames of light.

Carrying a worn-out mat, a bundle, an old cotton quilt tied with hemp rope, these things, in Ah Shun's resurrected life, began to become acquainted with [new companions].

XX Store was the most famous department store on a bustling street in X Port.

There, from the time of [opening the gate] in the morning to the time of [closing shop] in the evening, fifteen hours were spent living the rigid life of a [shop assistant], with no opportunity to engage in lofty discussions. Although business at XX Store was sometimes relatively slow, the clever and capable boss would ask you to do some extra work, such as holding his one-and-a-half-year-old precious daughter, chopping firewood, or helping with… and so on. It was a strenuous three and a half months!

Alas, an addict whose marrow was being squeezed out and whose body was being sold in the gears of life!

The principle of [fortune and misfortune] in the world is sometimes laughably contradictory. Our young Ah Shun, through his diligent and thrifty work, never dreamed that he would be unemployed!

It was said that the unemployment was due to laziness, but Ah Shun seemed very indignant about this misfortune. Laziness was what he hated most. He understood that his unemployment was based on the ways of the world and human relations. He couldn't flatter, couldn't brown-nose. Unfortunately, his old boss loved flattery and brown-nosing. Ah Shun had failed!

As he lowered his head in shame, carrying a worn-out mat, a bundle, an old cotton quilt tied with hemp rope, he felt many cold taunts and hideous glares around him, which frightened him into quickly rolling out of XX Store!

On the way home, he walked heavily, sluggishly, as if lacking courage, on the smooth Water Gate Road.

The setting sun trailed its blood-red shadow, jumping into the brocade quilt of the clouds!

Dedicated to Young Women 277

— Ping

In a novel by a female writer, she said two sentences that represent the modern woman's philosophy of life: [Relying on youth and seizing pleasure] is their goal.

Indeed, everyone believes that in her two short aphorisms, she used camera-like vision to capture the inner workings of a segment of modern women without missing a beat, and then expressed it on paper. However, if we carefully understand these two sentences, many historical events have already proven that the philosophy of life of [relying on youth and seizing pleasure] is not only a guiding principle for a segment of modern women, but also a guiding principle for a segment of ancient women.

Speaking of early pleasure, as far as I personally know, there are no more than two kinds of thinking… one is spiritual enjoyment, and the other is material enjoyment. Artistic appreciation, natural response, and love's intoxication belong to the former. Pursuing carnal desire, the stimulation of smoking and drinking, and the looting of money belong to the latter.

If we study these shallow principles from the literal meaning alone, it seems that the enjoyment of the spirit requires a higher level than the enjoyment of material things… However, in fact, it is extremely wrong. In the whole world, everyone, regardless of whether they are male, female, old, or young, isn't opening their eyes wide, clenching their fists, and chasing desperately after the ass of material things?

Some philosophers believe that matter and spirit are two phenomena in the universe that are mutually causal. To seek spiritual pleasure, the first step is still to seek material satisfaction; otherwise, no matter whether you are perched on an ivory tower or leaning in the arms of a lover, you will still starve to death in three days if you are not given food to eat.

In our ancient Republic of China, men's status in society is more important than that of ordinary women in any field. In the present situation where education is not universal and women's occupations have not yet developed, economic power is almost entirely in the hands of men. Men can use their superior economic position to seduce women, deceive women, and make women succumb to their gold without resistance.

This deformed development, on the one hand, is certainly due to men's irrationality, and on the other hand, it is also due to women's excessive belief in the philosophy of life of [relying on youth and seizing pleasure], which results in a bad situation.

According to general opinion, a woman's youth lasts at most from the age of sixteen to twenty-six. In these short ten years, although a woman can proudly use the power of her youth to make men fall in love, admire, and achieve her goal of enjoyment, after ten years, her beautiful youth will gradually disappear with the passage of time, and in the blink of an eye, she will become an old woman with wrinkled skin and white hair. At that time, her beauty will be exhausted, and whether men still obey her will is still a question.

Therefore, I believe that the pleasure gained by relying on youth is absolutely unreliable. Finally, I dare to advise women who are intoxicated with this erroneous view with a sincere attitude, hoping that you will never underestimate yourselves, and that you will not ruin your whole lives for the sake of temporary pleasure. Your only way out is to rely on your own efforts and drive everything in front of men.

The Son After the Divorce 278

— Ning Ying

The only [truth] in the world is children, so they don't understand adult matters at all. At this moment, when he often saw his mother talking and laughing with an unfamiliar father, he was filled with great questions.

[Mom, why hasn't Daddy come home for several weeks? Mom, why did Daddy make such a big fuss that day? Mom, I haven't had any candy for a long time. Mom, buy it for me.] He just wanted to eat candy, so he said a few silly things.

[I'll go out tonight and buy it for you.] She tasted the flavor of preserved plums.

[Mom, why doesn't Daddy come home? When will he come back?] The child always kept asking to the bottom of things.

Her eyes turned red, and she remained silent, pretending not to hear. He seemed puzzled. Why did his mother's eyes turn red and not say anything when his father was mentioned? Why did that man who came often want me to call him Dad?

[Mom, why does that man who comes every night want me to call him Dad? My dad buys me candy, wears glasses, and wears clothes like foreigners. Ling'er from next door called me Dad too, and you and Dad laughed at her for having two dads? Mom, how can I have two dads?]

[Child, don't be nosy. You're little, you don't know.] She said shyly, as if thorns were on her back.

His question was still an incomprehensible question. He also remembered sleeping with his parents on that big brass bed before. Why did they make him sleep alone on the sofa now? He spoke again:

[Mom, how can you sleep with that man [sideways]? Didn't Dad say before that when a country cousin married a sister-in-law, the sister-in-law slept with another man in bed, and the cousin saw it, and he scolded her and beat her up! Dad said they got divorced later. Mom, what does divorce mean?]

[Mom, will Dad come back when school is out?] He asked again, questioning to the end.

At this moment, in her heart, how she had been naughty with her husband, how they had divorced in front of a lawyer, how the son had been given to her to raise, everything, like a movie projected into her eyes, plus her poor son's silly questions, she couldn't say the sour feelings! Only…

[Child, it's getting late. Shall we go out together to buy candy? What kind of candy do you want to buy?]

As soon as the child heard about the candy, he forgot everything and shouted as he jumped…

[Mom, I want to eat chocolate candy.]

[Ah!] In her answering voice, she led her son out of the door. He jumped and ran, already reaching the entrance of the alley. Suddenly, he saw his father wearing glasses and a Western suit like a foreigner. He hurriedly walked away without looking back. He went up, grabbed the corner of his father's clothes, and his active, clear little voice filled the air…

[Dad, why haven't you come back for a long time?] Then he quickly turned his head and shouted to his mother…

[Mom, Dad is back. Ask Dad to buy my chocolate candy.]

Unemployment and Self-Cultivation 279

— Zhiqin

Unemployment is a common occurrence in life and an experience that should be had in the workplace. There is nothing to be surprised about or to be depressed about. Although encountering unemployment is an unfortunate thing, if you can use the period of unemployment to cultivate yourself, reflect on yourself, and it is easy to find past mistakes, you can quickly improve yourself and easily achieve significant progress. When you encounter an opportunity for employment in the future, you will be able to receive better treatment and happiness. The so-called "one who eats bitterness among bitterness becomes a man above men." I am a person who has experienced unemployment. The difficulties and hardships during the period of unemployment are, of course, no exception. The reason why I am now able to regain my employment is partly due to the help and introduction of friends, and partly due to my own efforts to cultivate myself during the period of unemployment. Friends who are unemployed, do you feel the pain of unemployment? Do you want to get a better job than before in the future? If so, then please pay attention to the following points.

First, during the period of unemployment, you must not be discouraged by unemployment, nor can you engage in bad pastimes because you are idle.

Second, often reflect on past wrongs, correct them, and repent.

Third, often read books that are beneficial to your desired profession to make up for insufficient academic ability.

Fourth, endure the pain of unemployment and develop good habits of calming down.

Unemployment is not absolutely unfortunate. If we can use the period of unemployment to cultivate ourselves, it is indeed a new opportunity for the unemployed. I deeply hope that compatriots who have been hit by unemployment will remember my words and put them into practice, so that what is lost in the east will be gained in the west, and we can wait and see.

Drama

War and Peace (4) (2) (4 acts) 280

— Ling Hong

Act Three: Ode to Peace

Financial Tycoon: Yes, every time the military and political authorities in North China raised funds, I have always been very dutiful. I am a very upright person. If I can do it, I will say I can do it, and do my best until I say I can't do it. Then there is definitely no way to do it. So when the minister talked to me about this issue the other day, I said there was no way, and there is still no way now.

Confidential Secretary: That's right. When Young Marshal Zhang was here, Mr. Zhang's efforts for the financial affairs of North China were truly admirable. Now, if Mr. Zhang is still willing to work for the government like that, I think it would be easy for Mr. Zhang to raise not only 20 million, but even more, 50 million, 100 million.

Peace Negotiator: Haha, that's right, that's right! Mr. Zhang's financial skills are well known and admirable!

Financial Tycoon: Thank you, Minister, and everyone for your praise. I am very ashamed. There is really no way to issue the 20 million war bonds this time. It is not that we doubt the government's credit, but that the banking industry in Tianjin can't come up with the money. No one will underwrite them. This is a matter of fact, not that I am unwilling to help.

Military Authority: Hey, I think this must be clarified. This is definitely not a matter of helping the government, but of doing things for yourselves. Why? The government has long been determined to resist Japan, even if it means one soldier at a time, and will continue to resist for a long time. Has Mr. Zhang forgotten? This request for a truce was first proposed by your banking industry, not that the government had the determination to stop the war first. If you now insist on saying that you are helping the government, then we don't have to truce; let's continue to see which side loses the most? Besides, it is the duty of our soldiers to defend our homeland and sacrifice our lives for the country. Are we afraid of resisting Japan? What a joke!

Entrepreneur: However, as far as I know, military setbacks are also one of the main reasons for the hasty truce. As the minister just said, we don't need to suffer unnecessary sacrifices.

Confidential Secretary: So, Mr. Liu means that our soldiers were the first to ask for a truce? That's a joke. Mr. Liu has always had great vision. Can Mr. Liu's cotton yarn still be as prosperous as before if we continue to fight like this and the market is so depressed? This is a very obvious fact.

Entrepreneur: Since Secretary He said so, then I have a very good reason to answer him. Yes, the market is depressed, which affects the development of Chinese industry, but on the other hand, from the standpoint of our industry, we can very well endure the current wartime sacrifices. Because we hope to expand this national war, and even recover the lost territory in the Northeast and take back our original market. At the same time, as the war continues, the boycott of foreign goods will naturally continue, which is of course an excellent opportunity for our industry. However, in fact, things cannot go as we wish. To be honest, Chinese soldiers cannot yet bear the heavy responsibility of protecting and developing national capital; although it is the duty of Chinese soldiers to defend the country. This is an ironclad fact that cannot be concealed by strong arguments. As for expanding overseas markets to foreign countries, it is even more of a dream for us. It is precisely because of this that it is better to stop in time and take another breath to prolong our lives. We cannot express our bitterness.

Modern Celebrity Paintings and Calligraphy 281

— Mr. Huang Binhong's Calligraphy (Brief Biography)

Mr. Huang Binhong has been touring famous mountains and rivers in recent years to enhance his poetry and painting drafts. Last autumn, he entered Sichuan and went up the river, passing through the Qutang and Wu Gorges to Bayu, and then went to Jiading via Luzhou and Xuzhou to climb Mount Emei to view the snow-capped mountains and the beauty of red leaves. He stayed in Chengdu for several months and had the opportunity to see a large number of ancient objects in public and private collections. In the spring and summer, he went to Qingcheng, climbed Xuanyuan Peak, came out of Guanxian, and viewed the Dujiangyan irrigation project where the river is divided and dikes are built. He passed Longquanyi, crossed the Jialing River, went down the Qu River, and returned to Chongqing from Hechuan. He returned to Shanghai from Sichuan and gained more than a hundred poems and nearly two hundred paintings. The other day, I went to visit Mr. Meng and was allowed to publish several landscape paintings of Sichuan, all of which are realistic works by the teacher.

Film Special Issue

Interview with Chinese Film Artists (8) (Continued from the 3rd of this month) 282

— Shaqi

(4) [Vitality] Director Shao Zuiweng (Part 1) 283

When mentioning this gentleman, I think all readers will be very interested. [Why?] If you ask like that… then I will say… [Have you seen [Vitality]?] Indeed, this work, [Vitality], is truly unforgettable for us.

Because of this, when I went to visit him, I subconsciously paid attention to him. I don't know if you have seen him, but I think it is easy for you to find a characteristic on his face… When his face is full of smiles, look! His left eye is big and his right eye is small. To put it jokingly, if Mr. Shao is willing to [sacrifice his looks] to star in a movie, as long as he has those eyes, I think he is very suitable to play a villain role.

For the sake of the readers' time and the value of the Shen Bao's space, the following is a record of his conversation. In a reception room full of film stills, he sat in front of me smiling, speaking Mandarin with a Ningbo accent…

[As far as the current style of Chinese films is concerned, most of them expose the darkness of the present society without seeking any solutions. In other words, they specialize in destruction without trying to build. As everyone knows, China today cannot withstand any more destruction. Therefore, I personally feel that Chinese films should be changed, should be improved, should be constructive, and should not talk about love. This has been concretely expressed since [Vitality].

[For example, in [Auspicious Land], which I am now starting to produce, it tells the story of a farmer who has a piece of land that is very good for farming, and a wealthy man wants to buy it at a high price. The farmer naturally cannot bear to move the bones of his ancestors buried in the ground. However, he is not superstitious. He wants the rich man to fund the construction of a small river to divert lake water into the village to save the drought as an exchange condition. This means breaking superstition and seeking benefits for everyone. Now that the countryside is so bankrupt, we should strive to build. This is my principle… to improve without destroying.]

From these simple words, we can easily see Mr. Shao's entire thought. Indeed, Chinese society is already so corrupt, shouldn't we build? This is absolutely true. But in theory, there should be destruction of the old before there is new construction. It is like rebuilding a house from the ground up. If we just repair [improve] the existing one, then the house with the shaky foundation will not be as safe as a rock after all. The so-called [improving without destroying] will inevitably waste the good intentions of benevolent gentlemen. However, in his position, he should say this, which we can prove in the following words.

[The Tianyi Company was founded entirely by me personally with my own capital,] he said… [Ten years ago, the capital was 10,000 yuan, and then it gradually increased to 100,000 yuan, plus 70,000 to 80,000 yuan in working capital. Now, including all kinds of assets, the total value is estimated to be about 500,000 yuan. In fact, it is making money. Tianyi Company has a characteristic, which is that it does not owe debts. For example, all materials are purchased with cash, which is a phenomenon that other film companies do not have.] (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of [Death Ray] Chandu the Magician 284

— Resident of Nanjing

The development of modern science is gradually eliminating the idealist concepts of religion and other superstitious beliefs. Therefore, all literature and art that emerge based on the spirit of science should relentlessly exclude all non-scientific elements in their themes and plots.

The true purpose of scientific inventions is to help humanity further overcome nature, that is, to create benefits for humanity. However, a small number of world rulers have used science – scientific inventions – to create wars and slaughter innocent people. The current race among imperialist countries to build warships, airplanes, and chemical industries is a clear example of using science to kill people. Therefore, under the war preparations of various imperialist countries, scientists are also constantly inventing all kinds of killing weapons, from tanks to poison gas. It is said that the death ray has also been invented.

Fox Company adopted such an invention event to produce a film. In principle, this should be a product that is imbued with the spirit of modern science, but in fact, it is far from it. The inventor of the death ray in the story initially gives us the image of an electrical engineer, surrounded by completely mechanized models. But in another place, there are many elements of ["Ghost-Obsessed Zhang Tianshi"]. We see magicians performing rope ascension, invulnerability to fire, and other Taoist magic, and Chandu returning home on a gust of wind. These two different spirits can actually be combined together. One can't help but admire the skills of the Hollywood studio bosses. But if the studio bosses of our country who made ["Investiture of the Gods"], ["Journey to the West"], and ["Seven Swordsmen and Eight Heroes"] were to see it, they would definitely say, "Hollywood is also learning from China."

The story does not have any special structure. It simply uses many dangerous and astonishing scenes to capture the audience's attention, such as Chandu's return home at the beginning, secretly going to Roxor's castle to inquire about information, the terror of many traps, Roxor's intimidation of Robert, etc. And these are all extremely bizarre. If a film uses such methods to attract people, then it is inevitably too empty and pitiful. Yes, capitalist culture is inherently extremely empty. Their authors can fabricate a story, create many thrilling encounters, and solve all these crises with vague and unverifiable magic and spells. Therefore, in the film "Death Ray," Chandu can be locked in an iron box and sink to the bottom of the Nile River, and then float to the surface and finally subdue Roxor, because he has magic. But if someone says, "Since Chandu really has the magic to subdue Roxor, why didn't he eliminate him earlier?" The answer to this question is that our clever scriptwriters will say, "He hasn't committed enough evil yet." The clever screenwriters will say, "If that were the case, there would be no movie to make."

The actors' expressions do not have any outstanding features. June Vlaleik, who plays the daughter, doesn't have enough terrifying expressions. The comedic characters interspersed in the play are relatively better. The son's role is not necessary in this play.

In summary, this film is an extremely absurd, supernatural, and unfounded product. In this scientific century, it is anti-scientific, and it intentionally or unintentionally promotes magic. Magic is its method of solving all difficulties. Through this film, it can further deepen the feudalistic concepts of the semi-colonial masses, deepen their belief in the supernatural, prevent them from progressing, prevent them from believing in science, and make them more foolish and more paralyzed, easier to use and easier to control.

Review of The Devil's Brother Tra Diavolo 285

— Ling He

Laurel and Hardy's ability to attract audiences is unquestionable. Therefore, they have become cash cows for film producers. Now, in order to meet the urgent needs of people who are too tired of life, production has to be stepped up, and their comedies almost fill the film market.

Regarding their works, we always have the same feeling: superficial and lighthearted, and it is impossible to find a little more serious meaning. Compared with Charlie Chaplin or Sydney Olcott, this judgment is even more accurate. This is because their cultivation is shallow, and at the same time, life determines their will, and what the market needs is this. No, what people who are too tired of life ask of them is these superficial laughs, so they have to do it this way.

That being said, their works cannot withstand strict scrutiny, especially when they star in films at the same time. On the contrary, if they are purely used to create jokes, it may not be enough to increase the jokes in the work, because they can only make some superficial and boneless gags. Therefore, in this work, it is very appropriate for them to stand in the position of supporting roles and take on the task of clowns. However, there are still some absurdities, such as the smashing of the sedan chair and some of the wine cellar due to the impact of a cow. As for robbing others but being moved by the robbers and the big laugh at the back, they are all very good.

The protagonist, Dennis King, had a very good record in opera in the past. In this film, he plays the bandit Fra Diavolo, who is heroic and dashing. In terms of the plot, it is indeed very suitable. In addition, the aristocratic woman Selma Todd is also very capable of expressing the ugliness of an aristocratic woman, but some small details are a little too much.

What can we say about the story itself? Two people had their only money robbed by bandits, so they were angry and became thieves, impersonating the great bandit Fra Diavolo. Who knew they would meet this person, like the real and fake Li Kui in the Water Margin. But Diavolo did not kill them, but instead taught them to disguise themselves as servants and plot to steal the property of a certain aristocratic woman. As a result, the three were arrested and sentenced to be shot. Fortunately, fools have their own blessings, and finally a cow saved them from execution. It goes without saying that this story is far-fetched and unreasonable. For example, the capable bandit joins forces with two fools, and many soldiers with guns cannot kill a cow, which ultimately allows the prisoners to escape.

However, the focus of our criticism is not here, because many playwrights are not necessarily Realit, although current films should at least develop in realism. So what we are saying now is, why not bring the bandit to justice? In many American films, when they write about bandits, the result must be death under the ["selfless"] national law, or the bandit must repent and start anew, and get the national law's ["no blame for the past." But here, it is an exception to the former and the latter, and the bandits are allowed to roam freely. Then it can be explained that these bandits are robbing the rich to help the poor, but except for hearing this sentence from Hardy's mouth, it is completely absent from the screen. On the contrary, the author portrays Diavolo as suave and the fool as simple and innocent, which can win the audience's sympathy. Therefore, it is better to say that it is because they rob the rich to help the poor and should not die, than to say that they are trying their best to please the audience in order to win their sympathy.

However, this is an adaptation of a French opera. Whether the original play was also like this is unknown. At the same time, this adaptation of the stage play is very good, except for the scene where the bandit sings in the inn, which has a slight trace of the original play. This is of course because the film can be used very flexibly, which shows the director's brilliance. Although some of the jokes are inevitably vulgar, the tone of the whole play is indeed consistently lively and vivid. To be precise, this is a comedy that is meaningless but very interesting to perform, an opera that has no content but seeks to make the form interesting. Of course, this interest is of no value.

Modern Film Issue 5 Published 286

The only film publication [Modern Film], jointly edited by Liu Na'ou, Wu Yunmeng, Huang Tianshi, Huang Jiamo, Zong Chuigeng, and Chen Binghong at 190 Beijing Road, is the latest and most exciting periodical monthly publication. It has been published for four issues and has been well received by readers all over the country. The fifth issue was delayed in printing due to the accountants being overwhelmed by public and private matters, which led to readers from all over the country sending letters and telegrams. The society strived for excellence and did not want to be sloppy, and repeatedly revised the manuscript before it was completed. It has been published recently and the content is even more exciting than before. The copperplate illustrations have many new contributions. The text is concise and insightful. The number of pages has increased to forty pages. The price remains unchanged and is still sold at 10 cents per copy. The annual subscription is 2 yuan, postage included. Send 20 cents for postage and a copy will be sent immediately.

Payment Regulations 288

The library will issue payments from the 6th to the 10th of each month, and again from the 16th to the 20th, except for Sundays, from 2 to 4 pm each day. Please bring a receipt stamped with the same seal as the original manuscript to the accounting department to receive payment. If you are collecting for several months at once, you must provide separate receipts stamped for each month in order to attach them to the ledger. As for the stamping, regardless of the length of the article or the number of times you submit an article each month, please stamp each article in order to verify the seal when collecting payment. If you do not stamp, it will be considered a waiver of payment. Furthermore, the payment will be cancelled six months after the date of publication if it has not been collected by then, in order to close the account.

Messrs. Canlan, Rujun, Ludi, Luhuo, and others, we acknowledge with gratitude your contributions to the September film special issue. However, as the submitted manuscripts were not stamped, they will be treated as a waiver of payment according to regulations. If you wish to receive the payment, please send the seal to us as soon as possible, and come to collect it according to the above-mentioned payment guidelines. Sincerely, the editorial department of the Shenbao Film Special Issue.

Film Novel Three-Cornered Moon (8) 289

— Bolun

Ronald said disdainfully, "[I don't do that kind of office work]." Everyone was stunned. Ronald said to Elizabeth, "[You go and tell them]." Elizabeth reluctantly said, "[He doesn't want to do that kind of monotonous life. He's writing a novel now]." Kenneth said, "[Can't he put the novel aside for a few weeks?]" Ronald said, "[Put down my novel? That's impossible. Not even for an hour. It's my life]." Everyone was silent, but the unhappiness in their hearts was clearly written on their faces. Elizabeth's face was red, and she felt that they were too insensitive. She shouted angrily, "[He's a genius writer. If you send him out, you'll be destroying his talent!]" Kenneth said, "[Then what do we do?]" Eddie said, "[I don't understand why you're asking him to work. Doesn't he know our situation? I'm starving every day. If this goes on, I'll starve to death]." Elizabeth called out her brother's name and stood in front of him, but when she saw her brother's bloodless face, she felt heartbroken. She also felt that Ronald's suggestion was not wrong. Ronald's deep blue eyes looked at her, begging for her understanding. Elizabeth felt extremely uncomfortable. What should she do? Finally, she said to Ronald, "Ronald, we wanted to support you properly, but something happened at the factory today and I can't go back to work. Can you sacrifice for me?" Ronald sighed in resignation and asked, "[Where?]" So Stephen wrote down an address and gave it to him. Stephen added, "[Why don't you go see him now? He lives upstairs from his bookstore]." Ronald said resentfully, "[Elizabeth, I have to do this for you. Love is a trap that often harms oneself]."

Okay, Ronald left, and Elizabeth was extremely tired. She should stay awake, should plan how to find a job tomorrow, should wait for Ronald to come back; but she was extremely tired. She lay on the sofa and dozed off hazily. She felt Stephen standing in front of her, looking at her with a gaze of pity and love. She felt at ease, having someone as wise and brave as Stephen living in the same house; she felt in her dreams how reliable he was. She was in a daze when suddenly there was a loud bang that startled her awake. Then something seemed to roll down the stairs. Stephen rushed up the stairs in a hurry, and Douglas's big box rolled straight down, almost knocking Stephen down. When Stephen reached the top floor, Eddie was lying stiffly on the ground. Douglas said, "[I'm afraid he's dead]." Elizabeth came up immediately. She touched Eddie's face, which was as cold as ice, and the pulse on his head had also stopped. Elizabeth was shocked and shouted wildly, "[He's dead! He's dead!]" She hugged Stephen's arm tightly. Stephen wanted to push her away, but she hugged him even tighter. Stephen shouted, "[Let go!]" But Elizabeth's nerves were already deranged and she refused to let go. He used all his strength to push her away, and then opened his hand and slapped her heavily on the face. Only then did he wake her up. He silently watched Stephen gently pick Eddie up, carry him into the bedroom, and put him on the bed. (To be continued)
